Jamison Brereton

48 (489)
Agni (1тАУ10), Maruts (11тАУ12, 20тАУ21), Maruts or
Lin╠Зgoktadevata╠Дs (13тАУ15), Pu╠Дsan (16тАУ19), Maruts or Heaven and ╠г Earth or Pr╠еsni (22) ╠Б
┼Ъaс╣Гyu B─Бrhaspatya
22 verses: various lyric meters, arranged for the most part in prag─Бthas
Another curious hymn, made up of apparently disparate sections and composed in a variety of different lyric meters. The headnote above reproduces the dedicands suggested by the Anukramaс╣З─л, but they do not exactly fit the contents of the hymn. The first ten verses, dedicated to Agni, seem a conventional Agni hymn, the curios
ity being that it is not placed among the other Agni hymns. It is also metrically the most stable portion of the hymn, with paired prag─Бtha verses alternating br╠еhat─л and satobrс╕еat─л, save for verses 6тАУ8, where each verse has an extra eight-syllable p─Бda at the end.
The next three verses (11тАУ13) offer an odd interlude: the priestly associates of the poet are ordered to drive a cow nearby, who will give milk for the Maruts. Although the Anukramaс╣З─л identifies the Maruts as the dedicands of these verses, they seem incidental. The focus is on the cowтАФwhether as a metaphor for Bharadv─БjaтАЩs poetic inspiration, as a real cow meant to provide the milk to mix with soma in the ongoing sacrifice, or as both. This cow is reminiscent of the apparent cow in the extremely enigmatic verses of the Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra family hymn (III.53.15тАУ16), a hymn that occu
pies a similar place in its maс╣Зс╕Нala.
P┼лс╣гan is the subject of verses 14тАУ19, the heart of the hymn. As Geldner points out, the Bharadv─Бjas have a special relationship with P┼лс╣гan: Maс╣Зс╕Нala VI contains the only series of hymns devoted to that god (VI.53тАУ58). The first two verses of this section (14тАУ15) present a solemn, formal praise of P┼лс╣гan, who is compared to the great Vedic gods in his various qualities, despite his usual rustic and relatively lowly status. The two verses clearly form a prag─Бtha, though the second of them (vs. 15) has five p─Бdas (12 12 12 8 8) rather than the expected satobr╠еhat─л (12 8 12 8). After these two straightforward verses, notable only for the hyperbolic encomium of this minor divinity, there follow three verses (16тАУ18) containing a remarkable, intimate address to P┼лс╣гan, whispered into his ear (see 16ab), some of which, espe cially verse 17, is close to unintelligible. The translation of that verse given here is extremely provisional; what is clear is that the style and syntax are informal, and the poet probably uses idioms and popular sayings current in colloquial speech. Moreover, since it is whispered to P┼лс╣гan, it should be unintelligible to us. The final verse devoted to P┼лс╣гan (19), though it remains a 2nd-person address, returns to the high, formal style of the first two (14тАУ15) and is in br╠еhat─л. It should be noted that the three intimate verses have the same metrical structure as the three verses about the cow (11тАУ13) and share with those verses a certain idiomatic register. Each con sists of a sequence of kakubh (8 12 8: vss. 11, 16), satobr╠еhat─л (12 8 12 8: vss. 12, 17), and pura├╝с╣гс╣Зih (12 8 8: vss. 13, 18).
The final three verses (20тАУ22) are dedicated to the Maruts. The first two form another prag─Бtha (20 in the expected br╠еhat─л, 22 with an extra eight-syllable p─Бda at the end, like the extended satobr╠еhat─лs of vss. 6 and 8), while the final verse (22) is in anuс╣гс╣нubh. The reason for their position here is unclear. The final verse is enigmatic, as verses referring the MarutsтАЩ mother Pr╠е┼Ыni and their birth often are (cf. II.34.2 and especially nearby VI.66.1), and the hymn, having presented us with a number of puzzles along the way, ends with a final one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni and Maruts Renou treats this hymn in EVP XV (142-46).

English translation:

тАЬAt every sacrifice (honour) the mighty Agni with your reiterated praise, while we glorify him, the immortal, who knows all things, our dear friend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With your every sacrifice to Agni, and with your every hymn to his skill, weтАФthat is, IтАФhave proclaimed time after time the immortal J─Бtavedas, dear like an ally.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the two p─Бdas of the first hemistich as entirely parallel, with an instr.

─Бmreс╕Нita followed by a dat. of benefit/purpose. Others (Geldner, Renou, Klein [─Бmreс╕Нitas]) instead interpr. d├бkс╣гase as a infinitive or quasi-infinitive.

The 2nd hemistich has disharmony of number between the expressed subject, pl. vay├бm, and the 1st sg. verb ┼Ыaс╣Гsiс╣гam, a rare but not unheard-of phenomenon. Here we can link it to the ─Бmreс╕Нitas that dominate the vs., esp. the doubled preverb pr├бpra, in tmesis from the finite ┼Ыaс╣Гsiс╣гaс╣Г. Perhaps this serves as a sort of individuating feature: тАЬI after I тАж,тАЭ that is, тАЬwe.тАЭ This cannot be conveyed in Engl., though I admit that the published translation тАЬwe тАФ that is, I тАФтАЭ is itself barely English.

Griffith

SING to your Agni with each song, at every sacrifice, for strength.
Come, let us praise the Wise and Everlasting God, even as a well-beloved Friend,

Geldner

Mit jedem Opfer von euch und mit jedem Loblied wollen wir es dem Agni zu Dank machen. Wir wollen den unsterblichen Jatavedas, der lieb wie ein Freund, preisen.

Grassmann

Mit jedem Opfer, jedem Lied will eurem Agni dienen ich; Auf, lasst den ew’gen Wesenkenner preisen uns, als lieben Freund besing’ ich ihn,

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe son of strength, for he verily is propitious to us, to whom let us offer oblations as to the conveyer of them (to the gods); may he be our defender in battles; may he be our benefactor and the grandsire of our offspring.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The child of nourishmentтАФbecause he is inclined toward us, that one all on his ownтАФwe would ritually serve, for the bestowal of oblations.
He will become our helper in the prize-contests; he will become the strengthener and protector of our bodies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich of this vs. is problematic. First, the acc. phrase ┼лrj├│ n├бp─Бtam referring to Agni should be (and indeed must be) the obj. of d─Б╠Б┼Ыema тАШwe would ritually serveтАЩ, but this DIR.OBJ + VERB sequence is interrupted by a parenthetical nominal clause apparently referring to Agni in the nominative (s├б тАж ay├бm). Further, the make-up of the complex hin─Б╠Бy├бm is much discussed. As it happens, I devoted a brief article to just this expression (тАЬRV s├б hin─Б╠Бy├бm (VI.48.2) with a Return Visit to n─Б╠Бy├бm and n─Б╠Бn─Б,тАЭ Fs. H. H. Hock, 2013). There I suggest that the proper segmentation is *h├н n─Б╠Бay├бm, with the particle h├н, which has lost its accent in the confusion, the nom. sg. n─Б╠Бto n├бr- тАШmanтАЩ, a form otherwise not found independently until the Amarako┼Ыa, extracted from the old ─Бmreс╕Нita n─Б╠Б-n─Б тАШman after manтАЩ, used adverbially to mean тАШevery man for himself, on his ownтАЩ, plus the near deictic ay├бm. Alternative views are discussed in the art. cit.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who are the showerer (of benefits), mighty, and exempt from decay, you shine with (great) splendour; you are resplendent, brilliant (Agni), with unfading lustre; shine forth with glorious rays.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because, Agni, as a great unaging bull, you radiate widely with
your beam,
constantly flaming up with your untiring flame, o flame-bright one, shine bright with your bright lights.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The second hemistich has two alliterative etymological figures: c ┼Ыoc├нс╣г─Б ┼Ы├│┼Ыucac chuce and d sud─лt├нbhiс╕е s├║ d─лdihi. The second is esp. nice, with su- тАШgoodтАЩ as the first cmpd. member echoed by s├║ the independent particle.

Griffith

Agni, thou beamest forth with light, great Hero, never changed by time.
Shining, pure Agni! with a light that never fades, beam with thy fair beams brilliantly.

Denn du, Agni, der alterlose gro├Яe Bulle, erstrahlst mit deiner Flamme, mit nie ermattender Glut ergl├╝hend, du Reiner. Leuchte fein mit sch├╢nem Lichte!

Grassmann

Denn, Agni du, ein junger Held, ein grosser, strahlst mit deinem Schein; O lichter, leuchtend mit dem Licht, das nie verlischt, mit hellem Glanz ergl├дnze du.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou sacrifice to the mighty gods; sacrifice (for us) continually, for (sacrifice is perfected) by your wisdom and your acts; bring them down, Agni, for our salvation; present (to them) the sacrificial food, partake of it yourself.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You sacrifice to the great gods: sacrifice in due order with your resolve and wondrous power.
Bring them nearby for help, Agni. Bestow prizes and win them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a juxtaposes two 2nd sg. forms of тИЪyaj, the indic. pres. y├бjasi and the - si-impv. y├бkс╣гi, in separate clauses. This juxtaposition presumably accounts for the accent on y├бjasi.

In d the obj. must be v─Б╠Бj─Б, extracted from v─Б╠Бjot├б. Grammatically this should be a dual, but a dual is semantically unlikely (Oldenberg тАЬDual v─Б╠Бj─Б ist gewiss nicht anzunehmenтАЭ). Best to take it as a pseudo-/nonce neut. pl. For the phrase cf. (as Geldner does) I.48.11 v─Б╠Бjaс╣Г h├н v├бс╣Гsva; on this basis it is likely that v─Б╠Бj─Б is obj. of both r─Б╠Бsva and v├бс╣Гsva, although the position of ut├б associates it esp. with r─Б╠Бsva.

Griffith

Thou worshippest great Gods: bring them without delay by wisdom and thy wondrous power.
O Agni, make them turn hither to succour us. Give strength, and win it for thyself.

Geldner

Du opferst den gro├Яen G├╢ttern; opfere in der rechten Folge nach deiner Einsicht und mit Geschick! Mache sie geneigt zur Gnade, o Agni, spende und erwirke Belohnung!

Grassmann

Die grossen G├╢tter ehrst du, ehr sie nach der Reih’ durch deine Kraft und Herrlichkeit; Zur H├╝lfe schaffe sie, o Agni, nah herbei; nimm Labung an und schenke sie.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(You are he) whom the waters, the mountains, the woods, nourish as the embryo of sacrifice; who, churned with strength by the performers (of the rite), are genitive rated in the highest plural ce of the earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Whom the waters: yam ─Бpo adrayo van─Б piprati: water prepared to mix with the Soma, the vasat─лvar─л, the stones for grinding the Soma, and the wood for attrition

Jamison Brereton

Whom the waters, the stones, and the trees carry to term as the embryo of truth,

who is born, when he is churned mightily by men, on the back of the earth,

Jamison Brereton Notes

On p├нprati as тАШcarry to termтАЩ, a specialization of тАШcarry to the far shoreтАЩ, see comm. ad I.156.3, also in a birth context. Most take it as belonging to тАШfillтАЩ (Grassmann, Renou), while Geldner tr. тАШn├дhrenтАЩ and considers it a blend of the two roots тИЪpс╣Э (n. 5ab). Rather than assigning it to тАШfillтАЩ, I prefer to think that it participates in a word play with papra├║ тАШhas filledтАЩ in the next vs. (6a).

Griffith

He whom floods, stones, and trees support, the offspring of eternal Law;
He who when rubbed with force is brought to life by men upon the lofty height of earth;

Geldner

Den die Gew├дsser, die Steine, die B├дume als Kind der Ordnung n├дhren, der mit Gewalt von den M├дnnern gerieben erzeugt wird auf der Erh├╢hung der Erde;

Grassmann

Den Wasser f├╢rdern, Wolkenh├╢hn und W├дlder, er, des Opfers Spross, Der von den M├дnnern auf der Erde hohem Sitz durch kr├дft’ges Reiben ward erzeugt.

Elizarenkova

рдпрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рднрд╛рдиреБрдирд╛ рджреАрдкреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЙрднреЗ рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдЖ рдкрдкреНрд░реМ рдЖрдкреВрд░рдпрддрд┐ рд╕рдГ рдзреВрдореЗрди рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдзрд╛рд╡рддреЗ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рдзреВрдореЛ рд╣рд┐ рдореЗрдШрд╛рддреНрдордирд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рдгрддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдХрд╛рд░рдгрдпреЛрд░рднреЗрджрд╡рд┐рд╡рдХреНрд╖рдпрд╛ рддрджреНрдЧрдордирдордЧреНрдирд╛рд╡реБрдкрдЪрд░реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪрд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрд░реБрд╖рдГ рдЖрд░реЛрдЪрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдореЗрд╡рдВрдЧреБрдгрдХреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕реБ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рд╕реБ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рд╕реБ рдКрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╛рд╕реБ ред рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рдирд┐рд╢рд╛рд╕реБ рддрдордГ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрдХреГрддреНрдп рдЖ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рджрджреГрд╢реЗ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдГ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реАрд╢реНрдЪ рдЖ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ ред рдЕрд░реБрд╖реЛ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреБрдирд░реБрдХреНрддрд┐рд░рд╛рджрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рдкрд╛рджрдкреВрд░рдгрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рд╡рд╛рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who fills both heaven and earth with light, who mounts with smoke into the sky, this radiant showerer (of benefits) is beheld in the dark nights dispersing the gloom; this radiant showerer (of benefits) presides over the dark nights.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who has filled both world-halves with his radiance, he races to heaven with his smoke;
he is seen across the darkness in the nights, a ruddy bull among the dusky ones,
a ruddy bull toward the dusky ones.

Griffith

He who hath filled both worlds fult with his brilliant shine, who hastens with his smoke to heaven;
He made himself apparent through the gloom by night, the Red Bull in the darksome nights, the Red Bull in the darksome nights.

Geldner

Der mit seinem Glanze beide Welten erf├╝llt hat, er eilt mit seinem Rauch gen Himmel. Durch die Finsternis hindurch scheint in den N├дchten der r├╢tliche Bulle, erhellt die dunklen N├дchte.

Grassmann

Der beide Welten hat mit seinem Schein erf├╝llt, mit seinem Rauch zum Himmel eilt, Er zeigte durch das Dunkel in den N├дchten sich, den finstern als der rothe Stier.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпреЛ рднрд╛рдиреБрдиреЛрднреЗ рд░реЛрджрд╕реА рдЖ рдкрдкреНрд░реМ рдзреВрдореЗрди рджрд┐рд╡рд┐ рдзрд╛рд╡рддреЗ рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕реВрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╛рд╕реБ рдпрддреНрддрдорд╕реНрддрддреНрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╛рд╜рд░реБрд╖реЛ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд░реБрд╖реЛ рд╡реГрд╖рд╛ рдЖ рджрджреГрд╢реЗ рддрдорд╛рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдд рееремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) (рдпрдГ) (рдкрдкреНрд░реМ) рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ (рднрд╛рдиреБрдирд╛) рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЗрди (рд░реЛрджрд╕реА) рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ (рдЙрднреЗ) (рдзреВрдореЗрди) (рдзрд╛рд╡рддреЗ) (рджрд┐рд╡рд┐) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ (рддрд┐рд░рдГ) рддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрдХрд░рдгреЗ (рддрдордГ) рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдГ (рджрджреГрд╢реЗ) рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ (рдКрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╛рд╕реБ) рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБред рдКрд░реНрдореНрдпреЗрддрд┐ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдирд╛рдоред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрез.рен) (рдЖ) (рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рд╕реБ) рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рд╕реБ (рдЕрд░реБрд╖рдГ) рдЖрд░рдХреНрддрдЧреБрдгрдГ (рд╡реГрд╖рд╛) рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдХрдГ (рдЖ) (рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрдЧрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛рдГред рд╢реНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯреЛрдкрдпреЛрдЧрд┐рдирдГред (рдирд┐рдШрдВрежрез.резрел) (рдЕрд░реБрд╖рдГ) (рд╡реГрд╖рд╛) рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдХрдГ рееремрее

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖реАрдгрд╛рдВ рдордиреЛрд░рдкрддреНрдпрднреВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧреГрд╣рдкрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕рд┐ рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рднрд╡рд╕рд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рдпрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда рдпреБрд╡рддрдорд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ рдЕрддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╢рддрдВ рд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдГ рд╢рддрдВ рд╣реЗрдордиреНрддрд╛рдиреН рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕рд░рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдореЗрджреНрдзрд╛рд░рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧрд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рдХреГрддрд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдорд╛рдВ рд╢рддрдВ рд╢рддреЗрди рд╢рддрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХреИрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреИрдГ рдЕрдВрд╣рд╕рдГ рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рддреН рдЖрд╣рдиреНрддреБрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ рд░рдХреНрд╖ ред рдпреЗ рдЪ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ рджрджрддрд┐ рдзрдирдВ рддрд╡ рд╕рдорд┐рдиреНрдзрдирд╕реНрдп рдХрд░реНрддрд░рд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рдкрд╛рд╣рд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, are the lord of the dwelling, and of all men the descendants of Manu; protect me, youngest (of the gods), when kindling you, with a hundred defences against iniquity; (grant me) a hundred winters, (as well as to those) who bestow gifts upon your worshippers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The lord of the dwelling: gс╣Ыhapati, master or protector of the house

Jamison Brereton

You are houselord of all the clans stemming from Manu, o Agni. With your hundred strongholds, o youngest one, protect your kindler from narrow straits for a hundred winters,
and protect those who give to your praisers.

Griffith

Thou art the Lord of house and home of all the tribes, O Agni, of all tribes of men.
Guard with a hundred forts thy kindler from distress, through hundred winters, Youngest God! and those who make thy singers rich.

English translation:

тАЬWonderful (Agni), giver of dwellings, encourage us by (your) protection, and (the gift of) riches, for you are he conveyer, Agni, of this wealth; quickly bestow permanence upon our progeny.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You good one, conspicuous by your help, impel bounties to us. Of this wealth here you are the charioteer, Agni. Find a ford for our progeny.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although ┼лty─Б╠Бcould be taken with the impv., the instr. of ┼лt├н- has a robust relationship with citr├б- elsewhere (e.g. I.172.1, II.17.8, IV.23.2, VI.10.5, VI.26.5).

vid─Б╠Бin the Saс╣Гhit─Б text can represent either a lengthened form of the impv.

vida or a subj. vid─Б╠Бс╕е (so Pp., also Grassmann, Lubotsky). Both Geldner and Renou tr. as an impv. (as do I), which fits the imperatival tone of the hymn better than a subjunctive.; see esp.

parallel codaya in b. Although neither Grassmann nor Lubotsky gives other imperatives to this stem, most of the forms analyzed as vid─Б╠Бс╕е are better taken as imperatives like this one (e.g., I.36.14, 71.7, VIII.61.7).

The particle t├║, which ordinarily takes standard 2nd position, is out of place here. The same sequence, tuc├й t├║ naс╕е, is also found in VIII.27.14, where it is also out of place. I have no explanation.

Griffith

Wonderful, with thy favouring help, send us thy bounties, gracious Lord.
Thou art the Charioteer, Agni, of earthly wealth: find rest and safety for our seed.

Geldner

Sporne, du G├╝tiger, durch Hilfe wunderbar, f├╝r uns die Freigebigkeit an. Du bist der Wagenfahrer dieses Reichtums, mach doch f├╝r unseren Samen einen festen Grund ausfindig!

Grassmann

Durch deine Huld, o strahlender, o guter, treib uns Sch├дtze zu; O Agni, F├дhrmann dieses Gutes bist du ja, schaff unserm Stamm denn gute Furt.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou protect with uninjurable, irremovable defences (our) sons and grandsons; remove far from us celestial wrath and human malevolence.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Deliver our progeny and posterity to the further shore, with deliverers who are undeceivable and not absent-minded.
O Agni, keep godly rages away from us and ungodly tangles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

p├бrс╣гi тАж partс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е тАЬdeliver to the further shore with deliverersтАЭ both continues the тАШfordтАЩ motif of the last vs. and picks up the same verb in 5b, where it has more restricted semantics.

P─Бdas b and c contain two different forms of тИЪyu тАШkeep awayтАЩ: the negated adj. ├бprayutvan- lit. тАШnot distant / absent, not inattentiveтАЩ and the impv. yuyodhi.

Note the chiastic figure h├йс╕╖─Бс╣Бsi da├нvy─Б … [├б]dev─Бni hv├бr─Бс╣Бsi ca. The inner terms, da├нvy─Б тАж ├бdev─Бni, are of course etymologically related, but, though both neut.

pl. a-stems, have different endings; the outer terms, h├йс╕╖─Бс╣Бsi тАж hv├бr─Бс╣Бsi are paired only by their initial h- and their neut. pl. s-stem ending -─Бс╣Гsi. The ca is of course misplaced: we would expect *├бdev─Бni ca hv├бr─Бс╣Бsi. Klein (DGRV I.53) says that ├бdev─Бni hv├бr─Бс╣Бsi тАЬis treated as an indivisible unit, and ca is therefore displaced to third position,тАЭ but this is a description, not an explanation. I would suggest that the poet didnтАЩt want to interrupt his pretty chiasmus. (The placement of ca also enables an iambic finish to the p─Бda, whereas the expected order would not, but I doubt if this is the major reason.)

Griffith

With guards unfailing never negligent speed thou our children and our progeny.
Keep far from us, O Agni, all celestial wrath and wickedness of godless men.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShe who yields immortal food to the powerful, self-irradiating band of the Maruts, who (is anxious) for the gratiication of the self-moving Maruts, who traverse the sky with (the passing waters0, shedding delight.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sumnair evay─Бvar─л: means of happiness, sukhahetubh┼лtaiс╕е;

Evay─Бvari = from eva, who or what goes, as a horse, or the water of mid-air, the rain, and y─Бvar─л, she who gies with, saha y─Бti ya, that is, who proceeds with rains, giving plural asure to others, anyeс╣г─Бm sukh─Бrtam vс╣Ыс╣гс╣нij─Бlaiс╕е saha gacchanti

Jamison Brereton

Who will milk out undying fame for the self-radiant troop of Maruts, who is in the grace of the precipitous Maruts, who goes her own way with benevolent thoughts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation renders dh├║kс╣гata as if it were a subjunctive (тАЬwill milk outтАЭ; sim. Geldner) to an s-aor., but the form must be an injunctive to a sa-aor., given the augmented forms ├бdhukс╣гata, etc., and the sec. ending -ta. Of course, the injunc.

could be used modally, but a presential тАЬwho milks outтАЭ might be better.

Griffith

Who, for the host of Maruts bright with native sheen, hath shed immortal fame like milk;
Whom the impetuous Maruts look upon with love, who moves in splendour on their ways.

English translation:

тАЬMilk for Bharadv─Бja the twofold (blessing), the cow that gives milk to the universe, food that is sufficient for all.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For Bharadv─Бja, once again, milk both a milk-cow yielding all milk and refreshment yielding all nourishment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner I take dhukс╣гata, identical save for the accent to dh├║kс╣гata in 12b, as a 2nd pl. act. impv., not a 3rd sg. mid. injunc. In a n. (13a) Geldner allows the possibility of the latter analysis, which would produce the paradox that a cow is milking a cow.

Renou opts for this latter analysis – the cow milking herself. Although I am always quick to see paradox in the RV, in this case I think the poet is playing with morphology instead, while bringing the final vs. of this 3-vs. sequence back to the 2nd pl. impvs. of vs. 11.

Note the direct object in balanced coordination, NOUN ca ADJ / NOUN ca ADJ, with both ca-s properly positioned (unlike 10cd above) and with each bahuvr─лhi epithet having the shape vi┼Ыv├б-CoCasam.

English translation:

тАЬI praise you, the (company of Maruts), for the distribution of wealth; (the company that), like Indra, is the achiever of great deeds; sagacious like Varuс╣Зa; adorable as Aryaman and munificent as Viс╣гс╣Зu.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Strong-willed like Indra, master of artifice like Varuс╣Зa,
gladdening and yielding lush nourishment like Aryaman, just like Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАФthat one will I praise for you, to mark him outтАФ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Despite the change in topic, sс╣Ыpr├б-bhojasam (a) responds to vi┼Ыv├бbhojasam, which ends the previous vs. (13c).

The enclitic vaс╕е in WackernagelтАЩs position in p─Бda a must wait for the verb stuс╣гe towards the end of d to find its syntactic niche. It refers, as usual, to the fellow priests on whose behalf the poet will praise the god. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬDiesen euren (Gott)тАЭ (sim.

Renou), attempting to find a function for it within the first p─Бda, is unnecessary.

This vs. contains four gods to whom P┼лс╣гan is compared and four adjectives. It is therefore not surprising that both Geldner and Renou distribute one adjective per god. My tr. differs: it honors the p─Бda boundary between c and d, which sequesters the twoadjective sequence mandr├бс╣Г sс╣Ыpr├бbhojasam in the p─Бda with Aryaman, leaving Viс╣гс╣Зu shorn of any epithet. This decision wasnтАЩt made only on the basis of the p─Бda boundary (which would be weak evidence), but also because sс╣Ыpr├б-bhojas- тАШproviding lush nourishmentтАЩ is an adjective more appropriate to the hospitable Aryaman than to Viс╣гс╣Зu. See Thieme, Fremdling 105, 143; M+A 83. By contrast, Viс╣гс╣Зu and P┼лс╣гan are often mentioned next to each other, almost as if interchangeable (e.g. VI.17.11, VIII.54.5, with the p─Бda-opening p┼лс╣г─Б╠Бv├нс╣гс╣Зuс╕е) and without descriptors.

The final infinitival ─Бd├н┼Ыe can be taken in a number of ways: Geldner (fld. by Scarlatta 221-22) rather whimsically as тАЬum (ihm) einen Wink zu geben,тАЭ while Renou instead gives тАЬpour attirer-son-attention.тАЭ I do not think it can be separated from the two forms of ─Б╠БтИЪdi┼Ы (including vs.-final ─Бd├н┼Ыe as here) in the nearby P┼лс╣гan hymn VI.56.1.

In that vs. I take the lexeme as meaning тАШdesignate (X as Y=epithet)тАЩ, and I think something similar is meant here: by giving P┼лс╣гan attributes and identifying him with various gods I’ve uniquely identified him.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI now (glorify) the brilliant vigour of the company of the Maruts, loud-sounding, irresistible, cherishing, whereby hundreds and thousands (of treasures) are bestowed collectively upon men; may that (company) make hidden wealth manifes; may it render the wealth easily accessible to us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Turbulent like the troop of Maruts, powerfully noisy, without assailantтАФP┼лс╣гan (I praise), so that hundreds,
thousands (of goods) he will heap together from the settled domains. He will make the hidden goods visible; he will make goods easy for us to find.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. not only continues the identification of P┼лс╣гan with other gods – here the Maruts, characterized by three different descriptors – but is syntactically dependent on the previous vs. and its verb stuс╣гe. It also contains the first mention of P┼лс╣гan himself (p─Бda b), at the end of the series of identifications.

The three adjectives, tveс╣г├бm, tuviс╣гv├бс╣Зi, and anarv─Б╠Бnam, must qualify both the ┼Ы├бrdhaс╕е тАШtroopтАЩ of the Maruts, a neut. acc. s-stem, in the simile, and p┼лс╣г├бс╣Зam, a masc. acc. -n-stem, in the frame. They seem to split the difference with regard to gender: tveс╣г├бm is of course ambiguous as to gender, but tuviс╣гv├бс╣Зi is neut. and anarv─Б╠Бnam masc. The latter is adjacent to masc. p┼лс╣г├бс╣Зam and separated by the p─Бda boundary from the neut. phrase, so it is not surprising that it would adopt a masc.

form. Moreover, a proper neut. acc. to this stem would be *anarv├б, which almost fatally obscures the 2nd member of the bahuvr─лhi. The same substitution of masc. acc. anarv─Б╠Бnam for expected neut. *anarv├б- is found with the very same neut. acc. referent ┼Ы├бrdho m─Б╠Бrutam in I.37.1; cf. comm. there. The expected neut. NA presumably underlies the them. adj. anarv├б-; see comm. ad I.185.3. GeldnerтАЩs and RenouтАЩs strategy of taking anarv─Б╠Бс╣Зam as only modifying Puс╣гan (e.g., Geldner тАЬden unerreichten P┼лс╣гan, der тАжтАЭ) is thus both unnecessary and probably wrong, given its application (not in a simile) to the Marut troop in I.37.1.

Griffith

Bright as the host of Maruts mighty in their roar. May they bring Pusan free from foes;
May they bring hither hundreds, thousands for our men: may they bring hidden stores to light, and make wealth easy to be found.

English translation:

тАЬHasten, P┼лс╣гan, to me; (repel), bright deity, (all) deadly assailing foes; close at your side I repeat your praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Close at your side: saс╣Г┼Ыiс╣гam nu te karс╣Зa = I celebrate your praise quickly at your ear

Jamison Brereton

Run up to me, P┼лс╣гan. I will announce close to your ear, o glowing one: тАЬEvil are the hostilities of the stranger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The little nominal clause agh─Б╠Бary├│ ├бr─Бtayaс╕е with its unremarkable sentiment (тАЬevil are the hostilities of the strangerтАЭ) may have been a popular saying, as itтАЩs found in the same form nearby in VI.59.8, an Indra-Agni hymn. It is not clear to me why P┼лс╣гan would care or why the speaker seems to impart it as a secret.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUproot not, P┼лс╣гan, the forest lord with its progeny of crows; utterly destroy those who are my revilers; let not the adversary ensnare me, as (fowlers) set snares for birds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Progeny of cows: k─Бkamb─лram vanaspatim: implies metaphorically the author of the s┼лkta, with his children and dependants; as fowlers: ev─Б cana gr─лv─Б ─Бdadhate veс╕е, even as sometimes they plural ce snares for a bird;

Gr─лv─Б = damam, j─Бlar┼лpam, a snare of the nature of a net

Jamison Brereton

тАЬDonтАЩt tear out the K─Бkamb─лra treeтАФpursue the taunts and make them disappear! And certainly donтАЩt (tear off the wheel) of the sun: for thus never could you give pursuit to the one who тАШputs the necksтАЩ (of the horses to the chariot-pole?).

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. seems to continue the poetтАЩs direct speech to P┼лс╣гan, and if it is meant to be a secret, it will remain so: as noted in the published introduction. the vs. is close to unintelligible. My interpr. differs markedly from those of others (or rather, from that of others: Renou and Klein [DGRV I.289] basically follow Geldner; Oldenberg, however, differs from them in cd, suggesting several other alternatives, none of which he stands behind).

The first p─Бda is deceptively straightforward, at least syntactically. It is a prohibition against uprooting a particular kind of tree. The tree name, however, is a hapax, with un-─Аrya phonology (k─Бkamb─л╠Бra- with plain b), and why this tree should be left in the ground is unsaid. As for the word, itтАЩs possible that itтАЩs a partial scrambling of P┼лс╣гanтАЩs epithet karambh─Б╠Бd- тАШgruel-eaterтАЩ (VI.56.1), but even if so, it doesnтАЩt get us anywhere.

The next p─Бda shows some word-order disturbances that cause me to interpret it differently from the standard and in fact to make a small emendation to the text.

The text as transmitted reads ├б┼Ыast─лr v├н h├н n─л╠Бna┼Ыaс╕е, with, apparently, a preverb in tmesis in 2nd position (v├н) and the particle h├н in 3rd position. Both of these would be quite unusual, though it must be admitted that in this kind of informal speech we might expect deviations from normal order. The h├н also suggests that the p─Бda offers the causal grounds for either the preceding clause or the following one. Geldner and Renou choose the former option, but I donтАЩt see how p─Бda a follows from p─Бda b as rendered by them, at least given our ignorance of significance of the K─Бkamb─лra tree. To address the word-order problems I suggest that instead of v├н h├н we read *vih├н, the 2nd sg. impv. to тИЪv─л тАШpursueтАЩ. (An asterisk should be inserted in the published translation before тАШpursueтАЩ.) Although this impv. is more often v─лh├н with long root vowel (as in nearby VI.50.2), there are several exx. with short root vowel (e.g., III.21.5, where the short vowel is metrically favored and perhaps guaranteed). Given the obscurity of this vs., it would not be surprising if the puzzled redactors split the syllables and endowed v├н with an accent as if it were a preverb. If my reading is accepted, we have either a sort of serial verb construction: тАЬcome on (and) destroy,тАЭ or simply a chronological series: тАЬpursue and destroy.тАЭ The latter is reflected in the published translation By my interpr. the redupl. aor. n─л╠Бna┼Ыaс╕е is accented because it starts a new clause. Unfortunately I cannot explain why we have a redupl. aor. injunc. rather than a caus. impv. (*n─Б┼Ыaya) following the 1st impv.

My interpr. of the 2nd hemistich diverges from the standard even more, taking KleinтАЩs tr. (DGRV I.289) to stand also for GeldnerтАЩs and RenouтАЩs: тАЬAnd may the sun not (shine) for even a day for the one who grasps the neck of the bird.тАЭ We all agree that m├│t├б stands for m─Б╠Б+ ut├б, with ut├б conjoining the two prohibitive particles in a and c.

Beyond this, anyone confronting this hemistich must deal with several textual problems: 1) the meter of c is disturbed; in fact Oldenberg calls it тАЬhoffnungslosтАЭ; 2) it is difficult to decide what underlies the transmitted sequence ├бha ev─Б╠Б; the Pp. takes ├бha as ├бhar, but, needless to say, this sandhi would be unusual; 3) ev─Б╠Бwith long final is almost always p─Бda- or clause-initial, as opposed to generally 2nd-position ev├б (see Lubotsky s.vv.). In fact, in MinkowskiтАЩs detailed treatment of the two forms (JAOS 115.3 [1995]: 388-400) this particular passage is тАЬthe only one possible counterexampleтАЭ (p. 391) to this rule of placement. (With Oldenberg, Minkowski floats the possibility that two syllables are missing after ├бha, producing an 8-syll. p─Бda, with ev─Б╠Бcan├б then p─Бda-initial in a 12-syl. one. Since it is impossible to know what those missing 2 syllables might have been and since, all things being equal, weтАЩd prefer a Satobс╣Ыhat─л vs. [see published introduction.], which would have 12 8, not 8 12, as its 2nd half, I will deal with the text we have.) In addition to these formal problems, there are a few crucial lexical ambiguities: 1) s┼л╠Бraс╕е can be nom. sg. of the thematic stem s┼л╠Бra- or gen./abl.

sg. of the athem. stem sv├аr-; 2) as noted above, the underlying form of ├бha is unclear: does it belong somehow to the тАШdayтАЩ word (├бhar, ├бhan-) or is it the asserverative particle ├бha? 3) v├йс╕е, which should be read as a disyllable, can be a case forms of the тАШbirdтАЩ word (v├н-), either nom. or gen./abl. sg., or a verb form to тИЪv─л тАШpursueтАЩ. The standard interpr. presented above chooses the first of each of those lexical alternatives; in all instances I choose the 2nd.

The standard tr., with тАШsunтАЩ as subject, supplies тАШshineтАЩ as the verb; no justification is given by anyone who so interprets it (as far as IтАЩve been able to find).

My interpr. attempts to find some clues in context. There are a few; whether they are false trails or not I cannot be certain. The first is the verb of p─Бda a, which is presented as parallel to p─Бda c by the m─Б╠БтАж m├│ta construction. The verb is ├║d тИЪvс╣Ыh тАШtear upтАЩ. Various forms of тИЪvс╣Ыh are found in the often puzzling тАЬwheel of the sunтАЭ myth, describing the ripping off of this wheel. Cf. I.130.9 s┼л╠Бra┼Ы cakr├бm pr├б vr╠еhat тАж; I.174.5 pr├б s┼л╠Бra┼Ы cakr├бm vrhat ╠е ─Бd abh─л╠Бke [=IV.16.2]; V.29.10 pr─Б╠Бny├бc cakr├бm avr╠еhaс╕е s┼л╠Бryasya. In two of these three passages the gen. sg. of тАШsunтАЩ is s┼л╠Бraс╕е. Although this is slender evidence, it is, at least, evidence (as opposed to the random fantasy of the standard tr.), and I therefore borrow the verb тИЪvс╣Ыh from p─Бda a and supply тАШwheelтАЩ as its obj., with a dependent gen. s┼л╠Бraс╕е. This is supported by a nearby passage in a P┼лс╣гan hymn, VI.56.3 ut─Б╠Бd├бс╕е paruс╣г├й g├бvi, s┼л╠Бra┼Ы cakr├бс╣Г hiraс╣Зy├бyam / ny a├мrayad rath─л╠Бtamaс╕е тАЬAnd yonder golden wheel of the Sun he set down in the тАШgray cowтАЩ – he the best charioteer.тАЭ (This is the same hymn that contains the form ─Бd├н┼Ыe disc. above ad vs. 14.) It is not at all clear what story that passage is telling, but we can see that P┼лс╣гan, who is our addressee here, changes the placement of a detached тАЬwheel of the sun,тАЭ with the sun-genitive s┼л╠Бraс╕е as here. The detachment might results from tearing the wheel off the chariot of the sun. This chain of reasoning accounts for my tr. of the first part of p─Бda c: тАЬAnd certainly don’t (tear off the wheel) of the sun.тАЭ I am taking ├бha as the particle, not a form of тАШdayтАЩ (though тАШdayтАЩ could be worked into that tr.).

Of course this interpr. does not solve the sandhi problem: we should expect ├бhaiv─Б╠Б.

But if a new clause begins with ev─Б╠Б, as I think it does, the unusual sandhi break would be more understandable.

Starting a new clause solves the problem of non-initial ev─Б╠Бnoted above. But what is the content of the clause? Like the standard tr., I take ─Бd├бdhate as a dat. sg.

pres. act. participle, with gr─лv─Б╠Бс╕е тАШnecksтАЩ as object. However, I do not think this refers to the neck(s) of a/the bird. Instead, as noted above, I take v├йс╕е as a verb form to тИЪv─л; given my emendation in p─Бda b to *vih├н, v├йс╕е to the same root would follow naturally (or as naturally as weтАЩre going to get in this vs.). Given its disyllabic reading, I take it as standing for *v├бyas, the 2nd sg. subjunctive to the root present. IтАЩm assuming that P┼лс╣гan wants to give chase to (or at least follow) whoever does whatever heтАЩs doing to the necks, and if he (P┼лс╣гan) tears off the wheel of the sun, he wonтАЩt be able to. As for gr─лv─Б╠Бс╕е тИЪdh─Б, I conjecture that this describes one action in the harnessing of horses to the chariot. Note тИЪdh─Б in VII.34.4 ─Б╠Бdh┼лrс╣г├║ asmai d├бdh─Бt─Б╠Б┼Ыv─Бn тАЬPut the horses to the chariot poles for him,тАЭ and recall that the horse Dadhikr─Б is тАЬbound at the neckтАЭ (gr─лv─Б╠Бy─Бm baddh├бс╕е) in IV.40.4. But the тАЬplace necksтАЭ phrase is open to multiple possibilities, none of which imposes itself.

There are a couple of grammatical loose ends in this extremely loosely constructed interpr.: 1) dative complements are rare to тИЪv─л, 2) v├йс╕е is accented, though thereтАЩs no obvious trigger for the accent. It may be that it borrowed the accent from my putative *vih├н, or that the implied causal dependency of the ev─Б╠Бclause (thus my тАЬfor thus never тАжтАЭ) induced it. Or that the redactors had no idea what this meant (a mental confusion we share) and took it as a form of тАШbirdтАЩ.

To lay out my reasoning in detail is, I realize, not necessarily to convince – but at least there is reasoning every step of the way. I challenge other interpr. to provide the same!

Griffith

Tear not up by the roots the Kakambira tree: destroy thou all malignity.
Let them not snare by day the neck of that Celestial Bird the Sun.

Geldner

Rotte nicht den Kakambira-Baum aus, denn du solltest die Afterreden zuschanden machen. Und nicht soll die Sonne auch nur einen Tag dem scheinen, der den Hals des Vogels packt.

Grassmann

Nicht reisse aus dem Stamm des Kakambirabaums; denn tilgen sollst die Hasser du, Nicht schwinde hin die Sonne dem, dess Hand des Vogels Hals ergreift.

English translation:

тАЬMay your friendship be unbroken, like (the surface) of a skin without a flaw, containing curds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Skin containing curds: said to be always carried in P┼лс╣гan’s chariot

Jamison Brereton

тАЬLet (us) have a partnership that keeps the wolf away, with you who are like a leather bagтАФ
an unsplit one that holds curds, a well-filled one that holds curds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take the comparison to be between the partnership and the leather bag (e.g., Geldner тАЬDeine тАж Freundschaft soll sein wie der тАж SchlauchтАЭ), but the partnership is in the nom. (sakhy├бm) and the bag is in the gen. (dс╣Ы╠Бteс╕е), as is P┼лс╣гan (te). Given the deep uncertainty of this part of the hymn, grammar is all we have to hold onto, and grammar tells us that it is P┼лс╣гan who is compared to the bag. For the partnership with P┼лс╣гan, see I.138.4fg.

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, agitators, especially to be adored, may your kind and true speech be our conductress; that plural asant (speech which is the guide) to desirable (wealth) for both gods and sacrificing mortals.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

For semant. ‘agitators’ maс╣Ыti go.l = churning stick; maс╣Ыt- = to turn over (Kota); cf. sindhumathya = produced at the churning of the ocean (Skс╣н)

Jamison Brereton

O you shakers, let (us) have the valuable guidance of a valuable one and let there be the liberal spirit
either of a god or of a mortal who has sacrificed, o Maruts who receive the forefront of the sacrifice.

Griffith

May the kind excellence of him the Kind, loud Roarers! be our guide,
Be it the God’s, O Maruts, or a mortal man’s who worships, ye impetuous Ones!

Geldner

Eines Trefflichen treffliche F├╝hrung und Gro├Яmut soll uns werden, ihr Sch├╝ttler, sei es eines Gottes oder opfernden Sterblichen, ihr opfersamen Marut;

Grassmann

Des lieben liebe F├╝hrung sei uns wonnig, ihr Ersch├╝tterer, sei Gott er oder Sterblicher, o Maruts, sei er Opferer.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhose functions spread quickly round the heavens, like (the light of) the divine sun, since the maruts possess brillian, foe-humiliating, and adorable foe-destroying strength, most excellent foe-destroying strength.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He whose acclaim goes around heaven even in a single day, like the god Sun,
the Maruts assume his vibrant power, his sacrificial nameтАФhis
Vr╠еtra-smashing power, his preeminent Vr╠еtra-smashing power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take the rel. cl. of ab as unconnected with the rest of the vs. But surely the y├бsya refers to Indra, as is made clear by the тАШVс╣Ыtra-smashingтАЩ references in de.

The adj. vс╣Ыtrah├бm, twice modifying neut. ┼Ы├бvaс╕е (d, e), is attributed to a hapax thematic stem vс╣Ыtra-h├б- by Grassmann (see also RenouтАЩs comm.), beside the very well-attested root noun cmpd. vс╣Ыtra-h├бn-. Although this analysis must be synchronically correct, I wonder if the form here has not been re-marked from the expected neut. to the root noun, which should probably be *vс╣Ыtra-h├б. However, Michael Weiss suggests that the neut.

could have been simply the sten form *vс╣Ыtrah├бn, which could be misheard as vс╣Ыtrah├бm. See also disc. of satr─Б-h├бm ad V.35.4 and also of anarv├бm ad I.185.3. The re-marking must already have happened and the thematic stem extracted before the composition of this passage, since the -am ending makes position in the cadence.

Griffith

They whose high glory in a moment like the God, the Sun, goes round the space of heaven,
The Maruts have obtained bright strength, a sacred name, strength that destroys the Vrtras, strength Vrtra-destroying excellent.

Geldner

Dessen Ruhm in einem Tage um den Himmel l├дuft wie der Sonnengott. Furchtbare St├дrke, opferw├╝rdigen Namen haben sich die Marut zugelegt, feindet├╢tende St├дrke, h├╢chste, feindet├╢tende St├дrke.

Grassmann

Die Maruts, deren Ruhmeswerk an einem Tag den Himmel, wie der Sonnengott, Durchl├дuft, empfingen hohen Namen, starke Kraft, feindt├╢dtende, gewalt’ge Kraft.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOnce, indeed, was the heaven genitive rated; once was the earth born; once was the milk of Pс╣Ы┼Ыni (pс╣Ы┼Ыnayai vai payaso maruto j─Бt─Бс╕е: Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 2.2.11.4) drawn other than that was not similarly genitive rated.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Once indeed was the heaven: sakс╣Ыd ha dyaur aj─Бyata utpadyate, once born i is permanent, sakс╣Ыd utpannaiva sthit─Б bhavati, or, being destroyed, no other similar heaven is born, na punas-tasy─Бm naс╣гс╣н─Бy─Бm anya tat-sadс╣Ы┼Ы─л dyaur j─Бyate; other than that was not similarly genitive rated: tadanyo n─Бnuj─Бyate = tataс╕е param anyaс╕е pad─Бrthastatsadс╣Ы┼Ыo notpadyate, after that another object or thing like that (object or thing) is not produced

Jamison Brereton

Only once was Heaven born; only once was Earth born.
Only once was the milk of Pr╠е┼Ыni milked. Another (of the Maruts) is not born after this.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half of this vs. is straightforward: both Heaven and Earth were born only once. The same тАЬonly onceтАЭ (sakс╣Ы╠Бt) appears in p─Бda c as well, but with the mention of Pс╣Ы┼Ыni things get complicated, esp. when p─Бda d is taken into account. The hemistich reads pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыny─Б dugdh├бс╣Г sakс╣Ы╠Бt p├бyas, t├бd any├│ n─Б╠Бnu j─Бyate. P─Бda c is unproblematically тАЬonly once was the milk of Pr╠е┼Ыni milked.тАЭ Geldner takes the milk here to be, symbolically, the Maruts; the point of the p─Бda is that Pс╣Ы┼Ыni тАЬward nur einmal Mutter.тАЭ (In this I think he is correct.) His d is тАЬNach dem wird kein anderer geborenтАЭ (sim. Renou тАЬ(nul) autre ne na├оt ├а la suite de (tout) celaтАЭ), both with an indefinite reading of any├бс╕е as тАШ(no) otherтАЩ; the published translation also has an indefinite reading, but limited to the Maruts – that is, the Maruts were born all at once and no other Maruts followed: тАЬAnother (of the Maruts) is not born after this.тАЭ But all of these interpr., however easily they go down, should be wrong. As I have demonstrated at length (тАЬVedic any├б- ‘another, the other’: syntactic disambiguation,тАЭ Fs. Beekes, 1997, pp. 11-18), indefinite and definite readings of any├б- are distinguished positionally: 2nd position any├б-, as here, is definite. (For a clear ex. see in the next hymn VI.49.3b with an any├б- тАж any├б- тАЬthe one тАж the otherтАЭ construction.) Our p─Бda d should mean тАЬthe other is not born after this.тАЭ This passage needs to be considered in conjunction with VI.66.1 m├бrteс╣гv any├бd doh├бse p─лp─Б╠Бya, sakс╣Ы╠Бc chukr├бс╣Г dudhe pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnir ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е, whose 2nd p─Бda is very close to our p─Бda c. VI.66.1 has an implicit any├б- тАж any├б- construction: the any├бd in the 1st p─Бda refers to Pс╣Ы┼ЫniтАЩs udder and is contrasted with the ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е in the 2nd p─Бda, which invites a reading with a second *any├бd. The published translation renders this тАЬwhile the one stays swollen to give milk to mortals, only once did Pr╠е┼Ыni milk the gleaming (milk/semen) from (the other) udder.тАЭ 66.1 is only limited help, however. Although its 2nd p─Бda is, as just noted, semantically and formulaically very comparable to our first, and its first p─Бda contains a form of any├б- as our 2nd one does, there are several important discrepancies: the any├б- in VI.66.1 is neut. and therefore pairs easily with the ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е of the following p─Бda, but our passage contains a masc. any├бс╕е which cannot be directly referred to the (neut.) milked p├бyaс╕е of the preceding passage nor to Pс╣Ы┼ЫniтАЩs (neut.) udder, which must be lurking in the passage too. Moreover, though the sakс╣Ы╠Бt p─Бdas of our vs. (abc) refer to a discrete event in the past, the verb of d, the any├бp─Бda, is present (├бnu j─Бyate).

I can see two ways of handling this problematic p─Бda, an easy one and a hard one. In the easy one I ignore my own rule about any├б- placement and take any├бс╕е as indefinite, with a tr. similar to Geldner/Renou: тАЬno other is born following thisтАЭ / тАЬanother is not born following this.тАЭ The published translation тАЬAnother (of the Maruts) is not born after thisтАЭ was adapted from von Bradke (Fs. Roth 118) and was an attempt to limit the scope of indefinite тАШotherтАЩ to тАЬother MarutsтАЭ and therefore wring a semi-definite sense out of it. But thatтАЩs a cop-out: itтАЩs still indefinite, and the more general rendering of Geldner/Renou may be more satisfactory if we are going the indefinite route.

Although this is the easier alternative, I am not at all sure itтАЩs the wrong one – though IтАЩm reluctant to toss out the any├б- rule without a struggle. The harder way makes reference to yet another desperate Pс╣Ы┼Ыni udder passage, this one II.34.2: rudr├│ y├бd vo marutaс╕е тАж, vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б╠Бjani pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыny─Бс╕е ┼Ыukr├б ┼л╠Бdhani тАЬwhen Rudra was begotten for you as the blazing bullish (semen = rain?) in the udder of Pr╠е┼Ыni, o Maruts.тАЭ For the difficulties of this passage and my interpr. of it, see comm. ad loc. The passage refers, in my view, to the birth (or a birth) of the MarutsтАЩ father Rudra, which тАЬbirthтАЭ then led to the birth of the Maruts. Acdg. to this passage, Rudra took shape (тАЬwas bornтАЭ) as тАЬbullish semenтАЭ in Pс╣Ы┼ЫniтАЩs udder. As I say in my comm. ad loc., тАЬIt is this semen that combines with Pс╣Ы┼Ыni to produce the Maruts; it can also, in naturalistic terms, be the rain in the thunderclouds that are Pс╣Ы┼ЫniтАЩs udder. This gender mingling and loss of distinction between the MarutsтАЩ bull-father (=Rudra) and their mother Pс╣Ы┼Ыni in the udder are also found, in somewhat different fashion, in IV.3.10d vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б ┼Ыukr├бс╣Г duduhe pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гnir ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е тАШthe bull as Pr╠е┼Ыni milked gleaming (milk/semen) from his (/her) udderтАЩ and in VI.66.1d sakс╣Ы╠Бc chukr├бс╣Г duduhe pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гnir ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е тАШonly once did Pr┼Ы╠е ni milk the gleaming (milk/semen) from the udder.тАЩтАЭ I now think it possible (though only that) that the masc. any├б- of our passage refers to Rudra (and/or his semen); in that case the referent is definite (as my rule requires), and the p─Бda means тАЬThe other [=Rudra] is not born after this,тАЭ in other words, the normal order of nature prevails: the father/semen was born in Pс╣Ы┼ЫniтАЩs udder before the sons, the Maruts, who resulted from the mingling of those essences and who were тАЬmilked outтАЭ of that udder – a bit of an anticlimax, to be sure: we wouldnтАЩt in fact expect RudraтАЩs birth to follow his sonsтАЩ. I am not sure that this is the correct way to interpret the passage, but it does conform to the known syntactic rules and also has suggestive connections with other troubling passages involving the same features: Rudra, his semen, Pс╣Ы┼Ыni, her udder, her milk, and the Maruts.

Griffith

Once, only once, the heaven was made, once only once, the earth was formed-
Once, only Prsni’s milk was shed: no second, after this, is born.

Geldner

Einmal nur ward der Himmel erzeugt, einmal ward die Erde erzeugt; einmal ward die Milch der Prisni gemolken. Nach dem wird kein anderer geboren.

Elizarenkova
